We can try to characterize the function f more generally.

Let N be a positive integer with at least three proper divisors. Let p be the smallest prime factor of N. Let d1 = p, d2 = min(p^2, q) where q is the next prime factor (if any), d3 = min(p^3, p*q, r) etc. Then f(N) = N/d1 + N/d2 + N/d3 = N * (1/p + 1/d2 + 1/d3). But note: This formula holds only if N has at least three divisors >1, i.e., τ(N) ≥ 4. For numbers with exactly three proper divisors, we have f(N) = d3 + d2 + 1, where d2 and d3 are the proper divisors themselves (excluding 1). So we need to treat that case separately.

Now, we want f(N) to be in S. So we need to find all N such that f(N) has at least 4 divisors.

Observation: For N that are fixed points (f(N)=N), we have N in S. So these are good.

Now, what about numbers that are not fixed points but f(N) is a fixed point? For example, N=72 gives f(72)=78, which is fixed. So N=72 is good. Are there other such N? We need N such that the sum of its three largest proper divisors equals 42. Let's denote the proper divisors in descending order: d_k > d_{k-1} > ... > d_1=1. Then f(N)=d_k+d_{k-1}+d_{k-2}=42. Since d_k is the largest proper divisor, it is N/p where p is the smallest prime factor. So d_k = N/p. Similarly, d_{k-1} = N/q where q is the second smallest divisor >1? Actually the second largest proper divisor is N/d2 where d2 is the second smallest divisor >1. So f(N)=N/d1+N/d2+N/d3, where d1,d2,d3 are the three smallest divisors >1. So we need to find all triples of integers >=2, d1<d2<d3, such that the sum of reciprocals is a rational number with denominator dividing 42? Actually we need N integer. We can use the formula: f(N)=N/d1+N/d2+N/d3 =78, where d1,d2,d3 are the three smallest divisors >1. Since d1 is the smallest prime factor, d1 is prime. Let's denote p = d1. So we can try to find N such that f(N)=78.

Let's try p=2. Then d2 and d3 are divisors of N that are the second and third smallest >1. Since N is even, the smallest divisor >1 is 2. The next smallest could be 3 (if 3 divides N), or 4 (if 4 divides N but 3 does not), or 5 (if 5 divides N and 3,4 do not), etc. We need to consider cases.

Case p=2, and 3 divides N. Then the three smallest divisors >1: 2,3, and then the next smallest could be 4 (if 4 divides N) or 5 (if 5 divides N) or 6 (if no 4 or 5). Since 2 and 3 divide N, 6 divides N. So the third smallest is min(4,5,6). So if 4 divides N, then d3=4; if 4 does not divide N but 5 divides N, then d3=5; if neither 4 nor 5 divides N, then d3=6. So we have subcases:

- Subcase A: N divisible by 2,3, and 4. Then d1=2,d2=3,d3=4. Then f(N)=N/2+N/3+N/4 = 13N/12 =78 => N=78*12/13 = 936/13 = 72. So N=72. Check: 72 divisible by 2,3,4? 72/4=18, yes. So N=72 works.

- Subcase B: N divisible by 2,3, but not by 4, and divisible by 5. Then d1=2,d2=3,d3=5. Then f(N)=N/2+N/3+N/5 = (31N)/30 =78 => N=78*30/31 = 2340/31 ≈ 75.48, not integer. So no.

- Subcase C: N divisible by 2,3, but not by 4 or 5. Then d1=2,d2=3,d3=6. Then f(N)=N/2+N/3+N/6 = N =78 => N=78. But N=78 is divisible by 2,3, and not by 4? 78/4=19.5, not divisible by 5? 78/5=15.6, so yes. So N=78 works, and it's fixed.

Thus for p=2, we have N=72 and N=78.

Now, p=2, and 3 does not divide N. Then the second smallest divisor d2 could be 4 (if 4 divides N) or some odd prime q (if N has an odd prime factor q<4? q=3? But 3 does not divide N, so q>=5). So we have:

- Subcase D: N divisible by 2 and 4 (i.e., divisible by 4). Then d1=2,d2=4, and d3 is the next smallest divisor >1. Since N is divisible by 4, it could also be divisible by 3? But we are in case 3 does not divide N. So d3 could be 8 (if 8 divides N) or 5 (if 5 divides N) or 6? Actually 6 would require 3 dividing N, so no. So d3 = min(8,5,? ) Actually if N divisible by 4 and also by 5, then divisors:2,4,5,8? But 5<8, so d3=5. If N divisible by 4 and also by 7, then d3=7 if 7<8? Actually 7<8, so d3=7. So we need to consider the smallest divisor after 2 and 4. That could be an odd prime q (if q<8) or 8 if no such q. So we have:

   - D1: N divisible by 4, and also by an odd prime q with q<8 (q=5,7). Then d1=2,d2=4,d3=q. Then f(N)=N/2+N/4+N/q = N*(1/2+1/4+1/q)=N*(3/4+1/q)=N*(3q+4)/(4q). Set =78 => N=78*4q/(3q+4). For q=5: N=78*20/(15+4)=1560/19≈82.105, not integer. q=7: N=78*28/(21+4)=2184/25=87.36, not integer. So no.

   - D2: N divisible by 4, but not by any odd prime q<8. Then the next smallest divisor is 8 (if 8 divides N). So d3=8. Then f(N)=N/2+N/4+N/8 = 7N/8 =78 => N=78*8/7=624/7≈89.1429, not integer. So no.

- Subcase E: N divisible by 2, but not by 4. Then d1=2. The second smallest divisor d2 is the smallest odd prime factor q (since 2 is the only even divisor, and 4 does not divide N, so the next divisor is an odd prime q, q≥3). Since 3 does not divide N, q≥5. Also, d3 is the next smallest divisor after 2 and q. It could be 2q (since N is divisible by 2 and q, so 2q divides N) or q^2 (if q^2 divides N) or some other prime r (if r<2q). So we need to consider possibilities.

   - E1: N divisible by 2 and q (q≥5), and also by 2q (always true if N divisible by 2 and q). The divisors: 2, q, 2q, ... Also, if q^2 divides N, then q^2 is a divisor. Since q≥5, 2q < q^2? For q=5, 2q=10, q^2=25, so 10<25. So the third smallest is 2q (unless there is another prime factor r such that r<2q, but r≥5? Actually r could be 3? But 3 does not divide N, so r≥5. If r=5 and q=5, then r=q, but if N has another prime factor r distinct from q, then r could be 5? Actually if N=2*5*7, then q=5, r=7. Then divisors:2,5,7,10,14,35. The three smallest >1:2,5,7? Actually 5<7, so d2=5, d3=7? But 2q=10 >7, so d3=7. So we need to consider the possibility of multiple distinct odd prime factors. So we need to handle general N with at least two distinct odd primes.

   - E2: N divisible by 2 and q, and also by r (another odd prime) with r<2q. Then the three smallest divisors >1: 2, q, r (if q<r? Actually we need to sort: if q<r, then d2=q, d3=r; if r<q, then d2=r, d3=q). So we have two subcases: q<r or r<q. But we can just consider the set of smallest divisors.

   - E3: N divisible by 2 and q, and also by q^2 (so q^2 divides N). Then divisors:2, q, q^2, 2q, ... Since q≥5, q^2 > 2q? For q=5, 25>10, so the third smallest is 2q (if 2q < q^2). So d3=2q. So f(N)=N/2+N/q+N/(2q)=N*(1/2+1/q+1/(2q))=N*(1/2+3/(2q))=N*(q+3)/(2q). Set =78 => N=78*2q/(q+3). For q=5: N=78*10/8=780/8=97.5, not integer. q=7: N=78*14/10=1092/10=109.2, no. q=11: N=78*22/14=1716/14=122.571, no. q=13: N=78*26/16=2028/16=126.75, no. q=17: N=78*34/20=2652/20=132.6, no. So no integer.

   - E4: N divisible by 2 and q, and also by 2q and q^2? Actually if q^2 divides N, then the third smallest is 2q (if 2q < q^2). So that's covered.

   - E5: N divisible by 2 and q, and also by another odd prime r such that r<2q and r≠q. Then the three smallest divisors are 2, min(q,r), max(q,r). So we have two cases: if q<r, then d1=2, d2=q, d3=r. Then f(N)=N/2+N/q+N/r. Set =78 => N=78 / (1/2+1/q+1/r) = 78 * 2qr / (qr+2r+2q). N must be integer and also N must be divisible by 2,q,r. Since N is divisible by 2 and q and r, it is divisible by 2qr. So N = 2qr * m for some integer m. Then the equation becomes 2qr m = 78 * 2qr / (qr+2r+2q) => m = 78 / (qr+2r+2q). So m must be an integer. Since m is a positive integer, we need qr+2r+2q divides 78. Also, q and r are odd primes >=5 (since 3 does not divide N). And q<r. So we can try small q,r.

   For q=5: then qr+2r+2q = 5r+2r+10 = 7r+10. We need 7r+10 divides 78. r>=7 (since q<r). Try r=7: 7*7+10=49+10=59, 59 does not divide 78. r=11: 77+10=87, 87>78, no. So no.

   For q=7: then qr+2r+2q = 7r+2r+14 = 9r+14. r>=11. r=11: 99+14=113>78. No.

   So no solutions.

   - E6: N divisible by 2 and q, and also by 2q and q^2? Already considered.

   - E7: N divisible by 2 and q, and also by r where r<q? That would be symmetric.

Thus for p=2, only N=72 and 78 give f(N)=78.

Now, p=3. Then the smallest prime factor is 3. So N is divisible by 3, but not by 2 (since if divisible by 2, the smallest prime factor would be 2). So N is odd and divisible by 3. Then d1=3. The second smallest divisor d2 could be 9 (if 9 divides N) or q (the next prime factor, which must be >=5). Since N is odd, the divisors are odd. So d2 is either 3^2=9 or the next prime factor q (q≥5). d3 is the next smallest after 3 and d2. We need f(N)=N/3+N/d2+N/d3 =78. Since N is odd, the largest proper divisor is N/3. The sum of three largest proper divisors is N/3+N/d2+N/d3. So we need to find N such that this sum equals 78.

Let's try to find possible N.

Case p=3, and 9 divides N (i.e., N divisible by 9). Then d1=3, d2=9. The third smallest divisor d3 could be 27 (if 27 divides N) or some other prime factor q (if q<27). Since N is divisible by 3 and 9, it is divisible by 27? Not necessarily; N could be 3^2 * m where m is not divisible by 3. Then the divisors: 3,9, and then the next smallest could be 3^3=27 if 27 divides N, or if N has a prime factor q such that q<27 and q≠3, then that q is a divisor. Also, if N is divisible by 3 and q, then 3q is a divisor. So we need to consider.

Subcase: N divisible by 9, and also by some odd prime q (q≥5) with q<27. Then the three smallest divisors: 3,9,q (if q<9? Actually q≥5, but q could be 5,7,11,13,17,19,23. Since 9>5,7, so d2=5? Wait, we need to sort: the smallest divisor >1 is 3. The next smallest divisor could be 5 if 5 divides N, and 5<9. So if N is divisible by 3 and 5, then the divisors: 3,5,9,... So d2=5, d3=9. So the ordering depends on the prime factors. So we need to consider all possibilities.

General approach: For N with smallest prime factor p=3, the three smallest divisors >1 are: 3, then the next smallest divisor (which could be 5 if 5 divides N, or 7, or 9 if 9 divides N and no smaller odd prime factor), then the third smallest. So we need to consider cases based on whether N has a prime factor less than 9 (i.e., 5 or 7). Since N is odd and divisible by 3, the possible prime factors are 3,5,7,11,... So we need to examine.

Let's denote the set of divisors >1. The smallest is 3. The next smallest is either 5 (if 5 divides N), or 7 (if 5 does not divide N but 7 does), or 9 (if 9 divides N and no 5 or 7). Then the third smallest is the next one.

We can try to find all N such that f(N)=78. Since f(N) = N/3+N/d2+N/d3, and N is divisible by 3, we can write N=3k. Then f(N)=k + N/d2 + N/d3. But N/d2 = 3k/d2, N/d3 = 3k/d3. So f(N)=k+3k/d2+3k/d3 = k(1+3/d2+3/d3). So we need k(1+3/d2+3/d3)=78. Since d2,d3 are divisors of N, and they are at least 3? Actually d2≥5? But careful: d2 is the second smallest divisor >1. Since N is odd and divisible by 3, the smallest divisor is 3. The next divisor could be 5,7,9, etc. So d2≥5. d3≥? Also, d2 and d3 must be divisors of N. So we can try to find integer k such that N=3k is odd and has the required divisors.
